RATING: 8
Renaissance-themed Euro that combines a variety of mechanics such as auction and tile-placement. Like a number of games of this type you're playing against the game rather than your opponents and interaction with other players is minimal (apart from the auction section). Like most of the best games of this type, you constantly feel as though there aren't enough turns to do everything that you want to, which in turn makes it a very strategic game as you can't afford to waste a move. This of course means that it's very unforgiving on mistakes and a single poor decision can mean the difference between winning and losing. Runaway leaders can also be difficult to reel back in.

RATING: 7
A gift from my 2006 Secret Santa (thank you Secret Santa!), a game I've had my eye on since I played it in a few different game groups.  A game that is truly best with 5 players, but in cases where the game isn't "ideal" (with newbies, or a learning game, etc.) fewer players is fine.  Sometimes dinged for being "multi-player solitaire", it is true that the actions themselves do not affect the other players.  Like Goa, this game shouldn't be thought of as "A strategy game that uses auctions" but rather, "An auction game that uses strategic actions."  The auction is the key (well, only) method of interaction, and it is not only in knowing how much a given item is worth, but, like in Power Grid, what item to choose to auction at the right moment.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Even with this being played with only 3 players I can tell it has staying power in my rotation. I'm sure it would be better with 4 or 5 but the odds are I won't get the chance to ever play it with 5. At least in the next five years or so until my son gets older. But there are so many interesting decisions in this game and it looks likely that it will not play the same twice in a row. Big thumbs up for this one.

Update: Played it with 4 and things are much much tighter. The bidding got pretty carried away at some points. It also seemed like the original distribution of the profession cards had a slight outcome on the endgame. I guess I could have bought some of the recruiting cards to off-set my disadvantage but there was never a right time to do so.

RATING: 9
Played twice now and enjoyed it greatly each time.  Both times played were with four players.  We missed one or two rules the first time through, but corrected the next game.  I think the bidding mechanism adds to the gameplay, although some items that attract bids in the first two turns are predictable.  (I take this as a challenge to develop a new early game strategy for bidding)  A fair amount of foreplanning is needed to account for the various professions and the various landscapes/buildings that will be needed given the limited play space for each person.  Overall, the learning curve can be a little steep at first, but I found the game to be good fun.

You can choose for diverse strategies since the mental factor is very high, them surer it is that they burst this strategy that you take weeks machinating to crush the rivals. #----0----# 

Las subastas: mi tema favorito. Y más aun cuando los recursos son tan limitados, la tensión se puede cortar con un cuchillo.

Se trata el  tema del “coste de oportunidad” de los negocios reales como nunca lo habría imaginado en un juego de tablero… un gran juego.

Puedes optar por diversas estrategias ya que el factor mental/matemático es muy alto, los más seguro es que te revienten esa estrategia que llevas semanas maquinando para apabullar a los rivales. Ya que tienes que tomar muchas decisiones en muy poco tiempo, y la obligación para reorganizar en cada momento tu estrategia hacen que el juego sea muy duro.

Los constructores, inspirar a los artistas, la interactividad entre los jugadores, la duración de los turnos,... los Bufones!

RATING: 5
Has that bland feeling that a lot of "classic" euros tend to have. I choose this strategy, so I have to make these moves. You choose that strategy, so you make those moves. If we all play our chosen strategies correctly, the victory comes down to who had the best luck during the game.

I give this a 5 because the gameplay is actually not that bad. It has bidding, a Tetris-like spatial element, and different end-game bonus conditions. I usually like those things, but they have mostly all been done better in newer, more fun games.

RATING: 8
I wish BGG has the option to choose "Dying To Play" here. I'd use it on this for sure.

2/22/13 - I finally got this to the table and it didn't disappoint. There are a lot of interesting decisions in every round. I like the puzzle element added into all the other planning elements of the game. I also like how players start the game out by getting most of their building rewards in money, but as the game progresses, that is shifted over to VPs. That makes for a very good timing element.

This is a must-have for Euro gamers. It is definitely a classic. And for good reason. Highly recommended.

RATING: 8
Very interesting auction game. In PoF, that didn't really seem to be the case -- part of that was an excellent rules explanation, but part is clearly the accessibility of the game, which I appreciated. RATING: 10
I've read many comments on how Puerto Rico is "the game" for their game group.  Ours is Princes of Florence.  Winning Princes of Florence in our game group is accomplishing something special.  It always gets played when someone calls for it, and a more competitive game can't be found.  The way this game punishes mistakes is brutal in a closely contested game.  Brilliant.  Sheer Brilliance.  There is downtime, it just normally concurs to when having to time to plan out your game is a good thing.  Plays slow early and quickly gains speed.  Just about perfect.



This game defines multiple paths to victory for me.  In our group, the only sure fire way to lose, is to use the strategy employed by the last victor.  All of the other players will realize what is going on, and up their bids making you pay too much.    The conflict between needing a long term strategy, but at the same time staying flexible to scarf up "The Game Winning Bargain" that always seems to pop up in some weird fashion.  Being able to integrate that buy into your plans is essential.

RATING: 7
Fun auction-based strategy game where players complete works for money/victory points. Each turn consists of an auction phase and then two actions. The 21 artists have things they like in common and if you can match these then each work will score more points. The 'jester' strategy, which we have recently found out about, highlights that the auction phase is the most crucial part of the round where you need to ensure you make your rivals' time as difficult as possible. I've read the game changes quite a bit from 2 to 5 players; with more players the game becomes a struggle for resources and competitors will need to adapt.

RATING: 7
This game had been sitting on my shelf for over a year, since I was a little tired of German boardgame mechanisms and had only purchased this game because of its good ratings and collectibility. RATING: 9
I have to admit, I was first drawn to this game because of its theme- trying to commission Great Works of Art to glorify Your City appeals to me in *many* ways.

Behind that veneer is an elegant, well-oiled system of a game that I have a decent but imperfect handle on, and will never pass up a chance to play, at least with 4 or 5.  Unfortunately, chances are very few and far between these days.  Probably the most "perfect" Euro I've ever played, possibly along with Acquire.  (Yes, I understand where some people think it's too dry, or too "solved", or mathematical or multiplayer solitaire or whatever.  Sure, it has less interaction than most of the games I love, but sometimes I'm in the mood for straight optimization with just a bit of auction screwage, and I love the theme far too much to ever find it "dry".)

RATING: 8
First play - 4 players - I finally managed to get into a game of this. Careful planning and shrewd bidding is the name of the game. Only 7 rounds to score points. The auction phase allows you to pick up a few things and then the main phase (2 actions) allows you to get building and other items. Showing off works each round and prestige cards (if you got any) score the most points. I managed to show 6 works in 7 rounds. I didn't get any prestige cards and that was my undoing. I wound up in a tie for first and I had the least money (tiebreaker). I look forward to trying to wrap my brain around this again. Second Play with 5 new players. I showed them the 4-minute video on the game and then explained it to them. I managed to pick up early cheap jesters while others fought over the builders. I won easily.

RATING: N/A
Wolfgang Kramer & Richard Ulrich; involves developing medieval and renaissance cities to attract various professions, which enriches the cities culturally. Each player is given a city grid and reference chart and attempts to gain the most victory points after seven rounds. While Princes of Florence can be played with 2 or 3 players, fans of the game overwhelmingly discourage doing so, insisting that at least 4 and ideally 5 players are needed.

RATING: 6

The general complaint of the game is that a player can't change his strategy halfway through the game, but I don't see that as a detriment; in the end, it's all about who can be the most economical with his cards.

RATING: 7
Base game 6/10, with expansion 7/10.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Everyone chasing the reprint of Wolfgang Kramer's Colosseum should cool their jets and grab a copy of The Princes of Florence. While I admit the dirt brown components and tea stained cards aren't nearly as sexy as the colorful tiles and toga wearing meeples of that other game, the play is so much richer here. The general feel is the same; grab a target card and then acquire all the required tiles to meet the card's demand, usually through auctions. Of course your opponents are doing the same and each type of tile is limited to one per auction round, so every auction is absolutely cutthroat.

Money is tight and this auctions are not the only place you need to spend it. You can straight up buy Prestige Points (VP's) at times, or use your cash to boost the output of your artist's creations. Who wouldn't want to support Da Vinci? of course do that and you may not be buying anything for a while. There's also a nifty Tetris puzzle you have to create with your buildings, which adds just enough frustration to make what to build and when to build it equally agonizing decisions.

Make no mistake, Colosseum is the family version of this game. If you are a heavy strategy gamer and you like Colosseum at all, you must play this game. Trust me, you'll never go back.

RATING: N/A
Strategy auction and tile placement to buy tetrus shaped palace items to place on your personal palazzo grid. Strategic placement of these buildings or landscape features will attract artisans to create better works.  Generate work points by tallying the list of tile placements against the list of on profession cards to get more auction money or convert to prestige.  The minimum to convert work points gets progressively harder with each round. Buy freedoms for artisans to create better works. Leverage scoring with personal objectives.  Respect the puzzle but too dry for my group.

RATING: 5
The positives include close games, tough strategic decisions, a pretty board, building up a city.  The negatives include a pasted on theme, and a completist underlying structure to the game (every variable is crossed nearly fully with every other variable). I'm accepting that I like the theme to be integrally tied to the mechanics. However, I like the mechanics to be careful, elegant, and interesting. The main intellectual activities are (i) deciding how much each auction is worth; (ii) trying to manuever the auction to get the maximum value relative to worth; (iii) deciding when to cash out your projects and when to invest in them further. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
A beautifully designed board game where players in renaissance Italy compete to hire scientists & artisans to perform great works.  The game is full of neat decisions, tight auctions, tension, and thoughtful fun.  

A nice feature of this game is that players cannot attack one another directly.  To win a player must get all the things they need for reasonable prices and see that the other players either can't buy or overpay for what they need.  The interaction between players is in the auction and in timing.  It is a much more subtle kind of game than Risk or Chess, and that is what makes it so excellent and enjoyable.

Spelers zijn vorsten in florence en proberen hun persoonlijke grond zo goed mogelijk in te richten om hun werklieden zo goed mogelijk te laten presteren.

Spelers proberen in een biedronde een aantal dingen te bemachtigen die alleen op die manier te krijgen zijn. Daarnaast kunnen ze ook werklieden naar hun hof halen en deze werken laten verrichten, dit levert uiteindelijk de overwinningspunten op die je nodig hebt.

De combinatie van bieding en een actiefase is er één die je weinig terug ziet en daarom dit spel al uniek maakt. Jammergeboeg nog nooit echt kunnen spelen met mensen die niet denken dat mijn manier DE manier is om het spel te winnen en dus zoveel mogelijk mij in de weg proberen te zitten.

RATING: 9.5
Played lots of times face-to-face (with 4 or 5 players), as well as on BSW (with 3 to 5). A game with a nice thematic feel, yet a very interesting gameplay as well. Various mechanisms interact, leading to an constant and difficult choices - both in the auction and in the actions phases. The main drawback of the game would be the huge learning curve: newbies are likely to be overwhelmed and unable to plan their purchases and actions far enough ahead, and will not know how to evaluate prices correctly. However, once this step has been overcome, the game becomes really, really interesting.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
I was looking forward to get this game onto the table. I wanted the Dutch edition, but as it is out of print, it became harder and harder to get a copy. Then we found an online store who had it on stock in Belgium. Last copy available they said. It didn’t matter to me, as I intended to get only one copy. The game takes 7 rounds to play, and each round consist of 2 phases. The 1st phase is the auction phase. An auction with 2 players is something I don’t like most of the time, and the same thing is the case in this game.  It just doesn’t work very well. Then phase 2, the action phase. Each player may take 2 actions. Possible actions are:

    Erect a building for 700 florins. Action may be played 2 times. Building has to be done according to the building rules.
    Make a person come to the palace for 300 florins.
    Get a freedom for 300 florins
    Get a bonuscard for 300 florins
    Complete a work.

While the game progresses, you’ll notice that the available space on your player board becomes smaller and smaller. Will the building fit on your board? Planning ahead is the big thing in this game. Your start with a plan, which you continuously adjust while your playing. It takes a while to play a game, but time flies as you’re playing, and you probably won’t notice the time passing by. Playing this game with two, makes it a lot easier then it will be with more players. It’s fun with 2, but I think it really shines with 4.

RATING: 8
Not bad, but probably a little overrated.  It's a fine game, but it's a bit solitaire-ish for my liking.  There isn't enough inter-player activity aside from competing during the auctioning phase.  I bought this one because many people who are somewhat down on Puerto Rico claim this is a better game.  They need their heads examined (or they just suck at Puerto Rico).

Editor's revision:  Ok, this game rocks.  My friend got blown out when he played this at WBC, so he basically told us we were missing out on some major strategy in this game.  We've since played it more and it has shot up on my list.  This is an awesome game, and I may try my hand at it in WBC next year.

RATING: 8
6/24/08 - Well shoot.  I guess I didn't want to like this game - perhaps because I wanted to feel like I was too good for it or something, but the fact is it's quite good.  It is also a pretty easy game to learn to play, it seems, which came as another surprise.  I think I've learned a valuable lesson here:  if 99% of people like something, it's probably for a good reason.  Rating raised from a 6 to a 7.

Previously:
I sort of feel like I'm at work when I play this game.  I have a bunch of stuff I have to do and elements to combine to produce a desirable outcome, but none of it is really all that much fun.  And I don't get a promotion afterward.
